## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables map directly to a constitutive law: stress (sigma) as a function of strain (epsilon) and temperature (T). Common models combine elastic response, nonlinear hardening/plasticity, and temperature-dependent softening via T-dependent moduli or multiplicative thermal-softening factors.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus (linear in T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness changes with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus (exponential softening/stiffening): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (thermally activated stiffness trend over wide T)
- Thermoelastic stress with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T + c2)) (thermal expansion produces stress-free strain shift)
- Nonlinear elastic (Landau-type polynomial): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate nonlinearity at larger strains)
- Hollomon power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic hardening after yield, log-log linear trend)
- Temperature-dependent power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * (T + c1)**c2 * epsilon**c3 (strength and/or hardening exponent vary with T)
- Voce hardening (saturating flow stress): sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (approaches a saturation stress with strain)
- Voce hardening with thermal softening factor: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon))) * (1 - c3 * T)**c4 (strain hardening plus multiplicative thermal weakening)
- Logarithmic hardening (dislocation storage proxy): sigma = c0 + c1 * log(1 + c2 * epsilon) (rapid initial hardening then diminishing returns)
- Johnson–Cook-like form without strain-rate term: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T)**c4 (empirical plastic flow with thermal softening)
- Exponential-in-T yield/flow stress trend: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) + c3 * exp(c4 * T) (captures strong temperature sensitivity of flow stress)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear sigma–epsilon at fixed T suggests purely elastic behavior; slope corresponds to an effective modulus E(T).
- A nonzero stress at epsilon = 0 often indicates a thermal-strain shift term like (epsilon - c*T) (constraint-induced thermal stress).
- Modulus or strength typically decreases with increasing T; structurally this appears as E(T) or strength multiplied by decreasing functions such as exp(-c*T) or (1 - c*T)**m over a valid range.
- Strain hardening commonly follows power laws; sigma ∝ epsilon**n indicates dislocation-mediated hardening in plastic flow.
- Saturation of hardening at large strain is captured by (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) terms (approach to a limiting flow stress).
- If thermal effects scale the whole curve (both yield and hardening), multiplicative separation sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T) is often effective.
- If temperature mainly shifts the baseline strength (yield stress) but not the hardening slope, additive separation sigma = f(epsilon) + g(T) is typical.
- Curvature changes (concave-to-convex) in sigma–epsilon can suggest combining polynomial elasticity at small strain with saturating/plastic terms at larger strain.
